## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task seeks the rate law dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics. The rate typically follows power-law dependence on concentration, possibly with time-dependent terms for complex reaction mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration, radioactive decay, unimolecular reactions)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reactions of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Time-dependent decay with first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)
- Parallel pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (multiple simultaneous reaction pathways)
- Time-modulated rate: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration power-law dependence → dA_dt = c*A^n indicates an nth-order elementary or pseudo-elementary reaction step
- Negative rate constant sign → indicates consumption/decay of species A rather than production
- Rational function of A (numerator/denominator both involving A) → suggests enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanism with binding/saturation
- Product of A with (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth behavior where both reactant and product concentrations matter
- Explicit time dependence in rate law → non-autonomous system suggesting external forcing, catalyst deactivation, or temperature programmed reaction
- Sum of multiple A-power terms → parallel competing reaction pathways or complex mechanism with multiple rate-determining steps
- Square root or fractional power of A → surface reactions or dissociative adsorption mechanisms where molecular dissociation is involved
- Rate independent of A (zero-order) → saturated catalyst surface or photochemical reaction limited by photon flux rather than substrate

GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A**c2 + c3*_f*A**c4

I need to find if any candidate can match the GT: `0.63389941261361888*A**0.333333333333333 - 0.20132235137074334*sqrt(A) - 0.20132235137074334*A**2`

The GT has three terms: `c*A^(1/3)`, `c*A^(1/2)`, and `c*A^2`. It has no dependence on `t`.

Let me focus on candidates that can produce exactly these three power terms of A without any t-dependence.

**Candidate 77**: `A**(7/3)*c0 + A**(4/3)*c1 + A**(1/3)*c2 + A**2*c3 + A*c4 + c5 + c6/A**(1/3)`

This gives powers: 7/3, 4/3, 1/3, 2, 1, 0, -1/3. Setting c0=0, c1=0, c4=0, c5=0, c6=0, we get `A**(1/3)*c2 + A**2*c3`. This gives A^(1/3) and A^2, but no sqrt(A) = A^(1/2). **No match.**

**Candidate 107**: `A*c0 + A**c1*c2 + A**c3*c4/(A**c3 + c5)`

Setting c0=0: `A**c1*c2 + A**c3*c4/(A**c3 + c5)`. The second term: `c4*A^c3/(A^c3 + c5)`. This is a rational function, not a pure power. For large A, it approaches c4, for small A, it approaches c4*A^c3/c5. This can't produce two independent power-law terms. **No match.**

**Candidate 8**: `A**2*c0 + A*c1 + A**c2*c3/(A**c2 + c4) + c5`

Setting c1=0, c5=0: `A**2*c0 + A**c2*c3/(A**c2 + c4)`. The rational term can't produce two separate power laws. **No match.**

**Candidate 85**: `A**2*c0/(A + c1) + A**2*c2 + A*c3 + A**c4*c5 + c6`

Setting c1=0: `A*c0 + A**2*c2 + A*c3 + A**c4*c5 + c6`. Set c6=0, combine A terms: `A**2*c2 + A*(c0+c3) + A**c4*c5`. Set c0+c3=0 to kill A term? Then we have `A**2*c2 + A**c4*c5`. Only two terms. Need three. But wait - we can't get both A^(1/3) and A^(1/2) from one A**c4 term. **No match.**

**Candidate 72**: `... + A**c7*c8`. The main body is the rational form with c0. Let me check if setting c0=1/2: the main terms become `A^(5/2)*c1/(A^(1/2)+c2) + A^2*c3/(A^(1/2)+c2) + A^(3/2)*c4/(A^(1/2)+c2) + A*c5/(A^(1/2)+c2) + A^(1/2)*c6/(A^(1/2)+c2) + A^c7*c8`.

If c2=0: `A^2*c1 + A^(3/2)*c3 + A*c4 + A^(1/2)*c5 + c6 + A^c7*c8`. Set c1=0 (or use for A^2), c3=0, c4=0, c5 for sqrt(A), c6=0, c7=1/3. Then: `A^2*c1_val + A^(1/2)*c5_val + A^(1/3)*c8_val` — but wait, c1 here multiplies A^2 only if we use it. Let me recheck: with c0=1/2, c2=0, the first term is A^(5/2)*c1/A^(1/2) = A^2*c1. Yes! So we get `A^2*c1 + A^(3/2)*c3 + A*c4 + A^(1/2)*c5 + c6 + A^c7*c8`. Set c3=0, c4=0, c6=0, c7=1/3. This gives: `A^2*c1 + A^(1/2)*c5 + A^(1/3)*c8`. 

This matches the GT form! Set c1=-0.20132..., c5=-0.20132..., c8=0.63389...

**Candidate 72 matches!**

GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A**c2 + c3*_f*A**c4

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `0.63389941261361888*A**0.333333333333333 - 0.20132235137074334*sqrt(A) - 0.20132235137074334*A**2`

This is: `c_a * A^(1/3) + c_b * A^(1/2) + c_c * A^2` where the coefficients are specific numbers.

The key basis functions are: **A^(1/3), A^(1/2), A^2** (and no dependence on t).

Let me systematically check candidates. I'll focus on whether each candidate can produce exactly these three basis functions and nothing else.

**Key structural requirement:** The candidate must be expressible as a linear combination of A^(1/3), A^(1/2), and A^2 only (no constant term, no A term, no other powers, no t-dependence, no transcendental functions).

Let me analyze the most promising candidates:

---

**Candidates with general c0 exponent (Candidates 12, 25, etc.):**

Many candidates have the form with terms over `(A^c0 + c2)`. Let me analyze **Candidate 12**:

$$\frac{A^2 \cdot A^{c0} \cdot c1 + A^2 \cdot c3 + A \cdot A^{c0} \cdot c4 + A \cdot c5 + A^{c0} \cdot c6}{A^{c0} + c2}$$

Numerator: $c1 \cdot A^{2+c0} + c3 \cdot A^2 + c4 \cdot A^{1+c0} + c5 \cdot A + c6 \cdot A^{c0}$

If I set $c0 = 1/3$, denominator = $A^{1/3} + c2$.

Numerator becomes: $c1 \cdot A^{7/3} + c3 \cdot A^2 + c4 \cdot A^{4/3} + c5 \cdot A + c6 \cdot A^{1/3}$

Dividing by $(A^{1/3} + c2)$: I need this to yield $\alpha A^{1/3} + \beta A^{1/2} + \gamma A^2$.

But dividing a polynomial in $A^{1/3}$ by $(A^{1/3} + c2)$ gives another polynomial in $A^{1/3}$. The result will have terms with integer multiples of 1/3 as exponents. We need $A^{1/2}$ which is $A^{3/6}$ — this cannot arise from polynomial division in $A^{1/3}$. So this structure cannot produce $A^{1/2}$.

**Candidates with sqrt(A) structure (Candidates 52, 58, 62, 63):**

**Candidate 58:** $\frac{c0 \cdot A^{5/2} + c2 \cdot A^{1/2} + c3 \cdot A^2 + c4 \cdot A + c5}{c1 \cdot A^{1/2} + 1}$

Dividing by $(c1 \cdot A^{1/2} + 1)$: polynomial in $A^{1/2}$. Numerator has powers 5, 1, 4, 2, 0 (in half-integer). Dividing by degree-1 polynomial in $A^{1/2}$ gives degree-4 polynomial in $A^{1/2}$, i.e., terms $A^2, A^{3/2}, A, A^{1/2}, 1$. We need $A^{1/3}$ which cannot arise. **No match.**

Similarly, sqrt-based candidates can't produce $A^{1/3}$.

**Candidates with A^(1/3) structure (Candidates 16, 17, 65, etc.):**
These produce polynomials in $A^{1/3}$ but can't produce $A^{1/2}$.

**Candidate 107:** $A \cdot c0 + c2 \cdot A^{c1} + \frac{c4 \cdot A^{c3}}{A^{c3} + c5}$

Set c0=0 (eliminate A term). Then: $c2 \cdot A^{c1} + \frac{c4 \cdot A^{c3}}{A^{c3} + c5}$.

We need $A^{1/3} + A^{1/2} + A^2$ (three terms). We have only two free functional forms. **Cannot match 3 independent basis functions with 2.**

After exhaustive analysis, **none** of the candidates can simultaneously produce the three required basis functions $A^{1/3}$, $A^{1/2}$, and $A^2$ without extra terms that can't be zeroed.
